        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel phosphide (Ni2P) hollow spheres were facilely prepd. via an org.-phase strategy using nickel(ii) acetylacetonate as a metal precursor, trioctylphosphine as a phosphorus source, and octyl ether as solvent.  A core/shell-structured Ni2P@C nanocomposite was grown in situ by employing oleylamine and 1-octadecene as capping agent and solvent, resp., and the hollow Ni2P spheres were homogeneously wrapped by an amorphous carbon shell.  The reversible capacity of the Ni2P@C nanocomposite after 50 cycles is 435 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C and 303 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C, resp., much higher than that of Ni2P (184.2 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C and 123 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C).  These improvements are attributed to the carbon shell, which can enhance the cond. of Ni2P, suppress the aggregation of active particles, and increase their structure stability during cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqtR2TKOJ13DbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh3CL9YacL9hg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhtl2nur%252FN&amp;md5=15aebff7cd172892a23c35ebb576a852</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C3TA13976J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fullwnwarth, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Darwiche, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Soares, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Donnadieu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Monconduit, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiP<sub>3</sub>: a Promising Negative Electrode for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A case study on fibrous porous SnO2 anode for robust, high-capacity lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Soo Min; Lim, Young-Geun; Kim, Jae-Geun; Heo, Yoon-Uk; Lim, Jun Hyung; Yamauchi, Yusuke; Park, Min-Sik; Kim, Young-Jun; Dou, Shi Xue; Kim, Jung Ho</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal oxides have attracted considerable interest as promising anode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to their high energy densities.  It is necessary, however, to resolve the foremost issue for them in terms of practical applications, relating to the large vol. changes during cell operation.  Herein, we report a SnO2 anode with a hierarchical fibrous porous architecture which was fabricated by electrospinning the Sn-precursor with poly(vinylpyrrolidone) and subsequent temp.-dependent pyrolysis processes, resulting in the distinctive morphol., featuring hierarchical fibrous porous structures on the microscale with numerous primary constituent nanoparticles.  The porous fibers are composed of uniform polycryst. nanoparticles (approx. 10-50 nm in size) and abundant voids in close proximity to the constituent nanoparticles.  By comparing with an anode contg. com. SnO2 nanopowder (with a size of &lt;100 nm), we found that the porous fibrous SnO2 anode featured superior rate capability, long-term cycling stability, and dimensional stability, which was attributed to the distinctive structural characteristics, which offered enhanced kinetics towards electrochem. reactions with lithium ions and space for alleviating the huge vol. expansion during charging/discharging.  These findings would pave the way for practical applications in LIBs with high capacity and long cycle life of transition metal oxide anodes that suffer from significant vol. changes during cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpLSxfgeqB1-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh3CL9YacL9hg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsFOlsL%252FJ&amp;md5=bf4974d2ccab7ccdd89bc205b75aee0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201404161"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Asiri, A.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon Nanotubes Decorated with CoP Nanocrystals: A Highly Active Non-Noble-Metal Nanohybrid Electrocatalyst for Hydrogen Evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qian; Tian, Jingqi; Cui, Wei; Jiang, Ping; Cheng, Ningyan; Asiri, Abdullah M.; Sun, Xuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of effective and inexpensive hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) electrocatalysts for future renewable energy systems is highly desired.  The strongly acidic conditions in proton exchange membranes create a need for acid-stable HER catalysts.  A nanohybrid that consists of carbon nanotubes decorated with CoP nanocrystals (CoP/CNT) was prepd. by the low-temp. phosphidation of a Co3O4/CNT precursor.  As a novel non-noble-metal HER catalyst operating in acidic electrolytes, the nanohybrid exhibits an onset overpotential of as low as 40 mV, a Tafel slope of 54 mV dec-1, an exchange c.d. of 0.13 mA cm-2, and a Faradaic efficiency of nearly 100 %.  This catalyst maintains its catalytic activity for at least 18 h and only requires overpotentials of 70 and 122 mV to attain current densities of 2 and 10 mA cm-2, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAcEpMutdD9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh3CL9YacL9hg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXot1Sgs7Y%253D&amp;md5=35dc0bfba605a71ac54f8b64ac4ea2b6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201600101"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tan, C.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improving the Specific Capacity and Cyclability of Sodium-Ion Batteries by Engineering a Dual-Carbon Phase-Modified Amorphous and Mesoporous Iron Phosphide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Fei; Tan, Clara Yi Jun; Gao, Zhiqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1054-1062</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMRA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2196-0216</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Based on the concept of the nanoconfinement reaction, a synthetic strategy is developed to construct carbon-coated iron phosphide (FeP) with an amorphous and mesoporous framework anchored on carbon nanotubes (CNTs).  The synthesis involves direct growth of FeOOH on the CNTs followed by silica coating, carbon coating, and subsequent treatments of low-temp. phosphidation and silica removal procedures.  During the synthesis, the silica layer is adopted to not only serve as a sacrificial internal spacer to increase the mesoporosity (311 m2 g-1 and 0.36 cm3 g-1) of the FeP framework, but also to provide a confined environment in guiding the structural evolution of the homogenous/conformal framework and topol. amorphous nature of FeP.  When used as an anode material in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the FeP-based electrode shows a utilization rate of 78 % for the active material and a reversible capacity of 415 mAhg-1.  Even at a higher c.d. of 500 mAg-1, a capacity retention rate of 90 % over 500 cycles is obtained with a capacity-decay rate of only 0.02 % per cycle.  The much improved performance of the FeP-based electrode in SIBs clearly demonstrates the potential of FeP to be used as the anode material in SIBs when it is engineered in a nanoconfinement environment to overcome its structural constraints.  In principle, this strategy can be adapted to engineer other transition-metal phosphide-based materials for energy-storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrhob2dXIaDRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh3CL9YacL9hg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XmvVSnurs%253D&amp;md5=b87d142360d08a67f3bfed67ecd9034f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.200600739"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Z. H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title"><i>In Situ</i> Growth of Mesoporous SnO<sub>2</sub> on Multiwalled Carbon Nanotubes: A Novel Composite with Porous-Tube Structure as Anode for Lithium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ growth of mesoporous SnO2 on multiwalled carbon nanotubes: a novel composite with porous-tube structure as anode for lithium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Zhenhai; Wang, Qiang; Zhang, Qian; Li, Jinghong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2007</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2772-2778</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel mesoporous-nanotube hybrid composite, namely mesoporous tin dioxide (SnO2) overlaying on the surface of multi-walled carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs), was prepd. by a simple method that included in situ growth of mesoporous SnO2 on the surface of MWCNTs through hydrothermal method utilizing Cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) as structure-directing agents.  Nitrogen adsorption-desorption, X-ray diffraction and transmission electron microscopy anal. techniques were used to characterize the samples.  It was obsd. that a thin layer tetragonal SnO2 with a disordered porous was embedded on the surface of MWCNTs, which resulted in the formation of a novel mesoporous-nanotube hybrid composite.  On the base of TEM anal. of products from controlled expt., a possible mechanism was proposed to explain the formation of the mesoporous-nanotube structure.  The electrochem. properties of the samples as anode materials for lithium batteries were studied by cyclic voltammograms and Galvanostatic method.  Results showed that the mesoporous-tube hybrid composites displayed higher capacity and better cycle performance in comparison with the mesoporous tin dioxide.  It was concluded that such a large improvement of electrochem. performance within the hybrid composites may in general be related to mesoporous-tube structure that possess properties such as one-dimensional hollow structure, high-strength with flexibility, excellent elec. cond. and large surface area.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGopOeHrZRQJ87Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhwnUWC2MgLMQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXht1ygurvE&amp;md5=1fcda2a9159053f7e2c29f6356115aca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502318"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although nanocryst. Si has a high capacity for the first charge it exhibits poor retention of capacity as a result of material degrdn.  A possible soln. to this problem is to use composite materials in which an electrochem.-active phase is homogeneously dispersed in an electrochem.-inactive matrix.  Carbon-coated Si nanocomposites were produced by spray pyrolysis and these reversibly store lithium with both a high capacity of 1489 mA-h/g and a coulombic efficiency &gt;99.5%, even after 20 cycles.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-based composite materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Stankovich, Sasha; Dikin, Dmitriy A.; Dommett, Geoffrey H. B.; Kohlhaas, Kevin M.; Zimney, Eric J.; Stach, Eric A.; Piner, Richard D.; Nguyen, SonBinh T.; Ruoff, Rodney S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature (London, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">442</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7100</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">282-286</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NATUAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0028-0836</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene sheets (one-atom-thick two-dimensional layers of sp2-bonded carbon) are predicted to have a range of unusual properties.  Their thermal cond. and mech. stiffness may rival the remarkable in-plane values for graphite (∼3000 W.m-1.K-1 and 1060 GPa, resp.); their fracture strength should be comparable to that of carbon nanotubes for similar types of defects; and recent studies have shown that individual graphene sheets have extraordinary electronic transport properties.  One possible route to harnessing these properties for applications would be to incorporate graphene sheets in a composite material.  The manufg. of such composites requires not only that graphene sheets be produced on a sufficient scale but that they also be incorporated, and homogeneously distributed, into various matrixes.  Graphite, inexpensive and available in large quantity, unfortunately does not readily exfoliate to yield individual graphene sheets.  Here we present a general approach for the prepn. of graphene-polymer composites via complete exfoliation of graphite and mol.-level dispersion of individual, chem. modified graphene sheets within polymer hosts.  A polystyrene-graphene composite formed by this route exhibits a percolation threshold of ∼0.1 vol.% for room-temp. elec. cond., the lowest reported value for any carbon-based composite except for those involving carbon nanotubes; at only 1 vol.%, this composite has a cond. of ∼0.1 S m-1, sufficient for many elec. applications.  Our bottom-up chem. approach of tuning the graphene sheet properties provides a path to a broad new class of graphene-based materials and their use in a variety of applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqiSXq1zKvbKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhwnUWC2MgLMQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XmvF2js7g%253D&amp;md5=f21ce86e81f2fd1e80ed987d0538188d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201603716"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, P. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Doped Graphene Ribbon Assembled Core-Sheath MnO@Graphene Scrolls as Hierarchically Ordered 3D Porous Electrodes for Fast and Durable Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yun; Chen, Penghui; Gao, Xu; Wang, Bo; Liu, Heng; Wu, Hao; Liu, Huakun; Dou, Shixue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7754-7765</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene scroll is an emerging 1D tubular form of graphitic carbon that has potential applications in electrochem. energy storage.  However, it still remains a challenge to composite graphene scrolls with other nanomaterials for building advanced electrode configuration with fast and durable lithium storage properties.  Here, a transition-metal-oxide-based hierarchically ordered 3D porous electrode is designed based on assembling 1D core-sheath MnO@N-doped graphene scrolls with 2D N-doped graphene ribbons.  In the resulting architecture, porous MnO nanowires confined in tubular graphene scrolls are mech. isolated but electronically well-connected, while the interwoven graphene ribbons offer continuous conductive paths for electron transfer in all directions.  Moreover, the elastic graphene scrolls together with enough internal voids are able to accommodate the vol. expansion of the enclosed MnO.  Because of these merits, the as-built electrode manifests ultrahigh rate capability (349 mAh g-1 at 8.0 A g-1; 205 mAh g-1 at 15.0 A g-1) and robust cycling stability (812 mAh g-1 remaining after 1000 cycles at 2.0 A g-1) and is the most efficient MnO-based anode ever reported for lithium-ion batteries.  This unique multidimensional and hierarchically ordered structure design is believed to hold great potential in generalizable synthesis of graphene scrolls composited with oxide nanowires for mutifuctional energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqh8xcBh8-tE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liH9WcMtz14WA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFenu7%252FM&amp;md5=632f9f9db962b375bfe78764a2077cd9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/jz201456p"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Iron is the cheapest and one of the most abundant transition metals.  Natural [FeFe]-hydrogenases exhibit remarkably high activity in hydrogen evolution, but they suffer from high oxygen sensitivity and difficulty in scale-up.  Herein, an FeP nanowire array was developed on Ti plate (FeP NA/Ti) from its β-FeOOH NA/Ti precursor through a low-temp. phosphidation reaction.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication and electrochemical characteristics of electrospun LiFePO4/carbon composite fibers for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Toprakci, Ozan; Ji, Liwen; Lin, Zhan; Toprakci, Hatice A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">LiFePO4/C composite fibers were synthesized by using a combination of electrospinning and sol-gel techniques.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-assembly of nano/micro-structured Fe3O4 microspheres among 3D rGO/CNTs hierarchical networks with superior lithium storage performances</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Jinlong; Feng, Haibo; Wang, Xipeng; Qian, Dong; Jiang, Jianbo; Li, Junhua; Peng, Sanjun; Deng, Miao; Liu, Youcai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanotechnology</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nano/micro-structured Fe3O4 microspheres among three-dimensional (3D) reduced graphene oxide (rGO)/carbon nanotubes (CNTs) hierarchical networks (the ternary composite is denoted as rGCFs) have been synthesized using a facile, self-assembled and one-pot hydrothermal approach.  The rGCFs composite exhibits superior lithium storage performances: initial discharge and charge capacities of 1452 and 1036 mAh g-1, resp., remarkable rate capability at current densities from 100 mA g-1 to 10 A g-1 and outstanding cycling performance up to 200 cycles.  The highly enhanced electrochem. performances of rGCFs depend heavily on the robust 3D rGO/CNTs hierarchical networks, the stable nano/microstructures of active Fe3O4 microspheres and the pos. synergistic effects of building components.  The systematic structure characterizations and electrochem. investigations provide insightful understanding towards the relationship between structure/morphol. and lithium storage performances, which may pave the way for the rational design of composite materials with desirable goals.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPEmFkEB_N1LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8wciep9NcdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXivFCmsro%253D&amp;md5=779c7dcc5b02a6f5b93c33a3231d7f56</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE03825H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Abdulla, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A composite cathode material consisting of (010) facet-oriented LiFePO4 nanoplatelets wrapped in a nitrogen-doped graphene aerogel is reported.  Such a composite possesses a 3D porous structure with a BET surface area as high as 199.3 m2 g-1.  In this composite, the nitrogen-doped graphene aerogel combined with its interconnected porous networks provides pathways for rapid electron transfer and ion transport, while the thin LFP nanoplatelets with large (010) surface area enhance the active sites and shorten the Li+ diffusion distances.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CNT@Fe3O4@C Coaxial Nanocables: One-Pot, Additive-Free Synthesis and Remarkable Lithium Storage Behavior</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Jianli; Wang, Bin; Park, Cheol-Min; Wu, Yuping; Huang, Hui; Nie, Fude</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">30</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">By using carbon nanotubes (CNTs) as a shape template and glucose as a carbon precursor and structure-directing agent, CNT@Fe3O4@C porous core/sheath coaxial nanocables have been synthesized by a simple one-pot hydrothermal process.  Neither a surfactant/ligand nor a CNT pretreatment is needed in the synthesis process.  A possible growth mechanism governing the formation of this nanostructure is discussed.  When used as an anode material of lithium-ion batteries, the CNT@Fe3O4@C nanocables show significantly enhanced cycling performance, high rate capability, and high coulombic efficiency compared with pure Fe2O3 particles and Fe3O4/CNT composites.  The CNT@Fe3O4@C nanocables deliver a reversible capacity of 1290 mA-h/g after 80 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA/g, and maintain a reversible capacity of 690 mA-h/g after 200 cycles at a c.d. of 2000 mA/g.  The improved lithium storage behavior can be attributed to the synergistic effect of the high electronic cond. support and the inner CNT/outer carbon buffering matrix.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJAo43LJS-m7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8wciep9NcdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXptFOitro%253D&amp;md5=55e7f69f1c8670b4a4286c13bf536a22</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/am502424j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, D.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Coated Magnetite Embedded on Carbon Nanotubes for Rechargeable Lithium and Sodium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Dae-Yeop; Myung, Seung-Taek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe3O4, carbon-coated Fe3O4, and carbon-coated Fe3O4 embedded on carbon nanotubes are synthesized via hydrothermal reaction.  SEM anal. reveals that particle size of the as-synthesized Fe3O4 ranges from 100 to 250 nm, whereas carbon-coated Fe3O4 ranges from 10 to 15 nm in diam. and is surrounded by a thin carbon layer derived from sucrose.  The surface modification by carbon is effective in prohibiting crystal growth during hydrothermal reaction.  The carbon-coated Fe3O4 is loaded on conductive carbon nanotubes during a hydrothermal reaction where the carbon nanotubes are added prior to the reaction.  Li and Na cell tests indicate that the carbon-coated Fe3O4 embedded on carbon nanotubes exhibits excellent capacity retention and a good rate capability compared to those of Fe3O4 and carbon-coated Fe3O4.  For both cases, the presence of conductive carbon nanotubes provides a conduction path of electrons and is thereby responsible for good capacity retention.  These results demonstrate the feasibility of dual alkali ions (Li+ and Na+) storage in inexpensive magnetite.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpZ4uG3923RcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXziGaiOli_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFSrtrjL&amp;md5=3de14c4c7483de25d251be832a9b54c9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.09.080"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Half-cell and full-cell investigations of 3D hierarchical MoS2/graphene composite on anode performance in lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Guanghui; Wang, Gang; Wang, Hui; Bai, Jintao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel 3D hierarchical MoS2/graphene (MoS2/GN) composite is designed by a facile one-step hydrothermal co-assembling method without using any templates.  SEM and TEM images show that the MoS2/GN flower-like particles are self-assembled by MoS2 nanoflakes and graphene nanosheets.  According to the hydrothermal method used and characterization results obsd., the formation process is proposed.  Electrochem. performances of the MoS2/GN composite as anode active material in Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) is investigated in both MoS2/GN//Li half-cells and MoS2/GN//LiCoO2 full-cells.  The MoS2/GN composite delivers high initial discharge capacities of 1240 mAh g-1 and good capacity retentions (about 80%) after more than 80 cycles in half-cells.  Furthermore, the assembled MoS2/GN//LiCoO2 full-cell delivers high initial discharge capacities of 1203 mAh g-1.  The excellent lithium storage performances of the obtained MoS2/GN composite can be mainly attributed to the designed novel structure of the composite.  The cross-linked graphene nanosheets, the anchoring MoS2 nanoflakes and the synergistic effects between them make the composite good cond., enough buffering space for the vol. change, and shortened ionic transport length.  This work clearly demonstrates that the MoS2/GN composite is a promising alternative material for anode in the LIB applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq1SBxs6HfMYbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXziGaiOli_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFajsLrM&amp;md5=f4352d4ffbe464f6bbfedd316c4f3b4d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2004.08.033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Okpalugo, T. M.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High resolution XPS characterization of chemical functionalized MWCNTs and SWCNTs</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Okpalugo, T. I. T.; Papakonstantinou, P.; Murphy, H.; McLaughlin, J.; Brown, N. M. D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2004</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">43</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">High resoln. XPS anal. of chem. functionalized multi-wall carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs) and single-wall carbon nanotubes (SWCNT) was done with ESCA300 (overall instrument resoln. of 0.35 eV).  Information to the degree of functionalization was ascertained by argon ion bombardment of the samples followed by XPS anal. to detect the functional groups, the percentage at. concn. of various elements present and whether or not the detected functional groups imposed a chem. shift on the CNT atoms.  The results show that true chem. functionalization was achieved and by argon ion bombardment can alter these functional groups relative to the C 1s carbon atoms of the CNT.  The choice of chems. used for functionalization, the techniques employed and the types of nanotubes treated are important factors in chem. characterization.  The carbon atom on the nanotube ring to which the functional group (atom) is bonded, the chirality of the CNT, the electronegativity of the functional group, the bond type and whether the CNT is single-wall or multi-wall, or cut (short) could play a role in detg. the chem. shift on the CNTs atoms.  These investigations are relevant to chem. functionalization of carbon nanotubes for various applications for example DNA sensors and other biomedical sensors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYnsG9ssliXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXziGaiOli_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2cXpslKgs7Y%253D&amp;md5=03a0482b2dd05539d5930d5e2409061d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-014-0531-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lei, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rationally Designed Carbon-Coated Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Coaxial Nanotubes with Hierarchical Porosity as High-Rate Anodes for Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Res.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1706</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1717</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rationally designed carbon-coated Fe3O4 coaxial nanotubes with hierarchical porosity as high-rate anodes for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Fei; Ma, Lingjuan; Sun, Qiang; Lei, Cheng; Lu, Anhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1706-1717</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe3O4 is a promising high-capacity anode material for lithium ion batteries, but challenges including short cycle life and low rate capability hinder its widespread implementation.  In this work, a well-defined tubular structure constructed by carbon-coated Fe3O4 has been successfully fabricated with hierarchically porous structure, high surface area, and suitable thickness of carbon layer.  Such purposely designed hybrid nanostructures have an enhanced electronic/ionic cond., stable electrode/electrolyte interface, and phys. buffering effect arising from the nanoscale combination of carbon with Fe3O4, as well as the hollow, aligned and hierarchically porous architectures.  When used as an anode material for a lithium-ion half cell, the carbon-coated hierarchical Fe3O4 nanotubes showed excellent cycling performance with a specific capacity of 1,020 mAh·g-1 at 200 mA·g-1 after 150 cycles, a capacity retention of ca. 103%.  Even at a higher c.d. of 1,000 mA·g-1, a capacity of 840 mAh·g-1 is retained after 300 cycles with no capacity loss.  In particular, a superior rate capability can be obtained with a stable capacity of 355 mAh·g-1 at 8,000 mA·g-1.  The encouraging results indicate that hierarchically tubular hybrid nanostructures can have important implications for the development of high-rate electrodes for future rechargeable lithium ion batteries (LIBs).                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Supercritical Carbon Dioxide Anchored Fe3O4 Nanoparticles on Graphene Foam and Lithium Battery Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Xuebo; Ma, Minhao; Zeng, Mengqi; Sun, Yangyong; Chen, Linfeng; Xue, Yinghui; Zhang, Tao; Ai, Xinping; Mendes, Rafael G.; Rummeli, Mark H.; Fu, Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Magnetite (Fe3O4) is an attractive electrode material due to its high theor. capacity, eco-friendliness, and natural abundance.  However, its com. application in Li-ion batteries is still hindered by its poor cycling stability and low rate capacity resulting from large vol. expansion and low cond.  The authors present a new approach which makes use of supercrit. CO2 to efficiently anchor Fe3O4 nanoparticles (NPs) on graphene foam (GF), which was obtained by CVD in a single step.  Without the use of any surfactants, the authors obtain moderately spaced Fe3O4 NPs arrays on the surface of GF.  The particle size of the Fe3O4 NPs exhibits a narrow distribution (11 ± 4 nm in diam.).  As a result, the composites deliver a high capacity of ∼1200 mA h g-1 up to 500 cycles at 1 C (924 mA h g-1) and ∼300 mA h g-1 at 20 C, which reaches a record high using Fe3O4 as anode material for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrnPdrllgQs6bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin5tcf6TWt2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVWitLjI&amp;md5=a5b68cf7cda8f0fba95a5f67e8920ddc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA03929K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, B.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hybrids of Mo2C nanoparticles anchored on graphene sheets as anode materials for high performance lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Beibei; Wang, Gang; Wang, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this article, we demonstrate a general approach to grow Mo2C nanoparticles of 10-40 nm on a graphene (GR) support through a simple and environmentally friendly carburization process.  The unique and special structural features of the Mo2C/GR hybrids including good structural robustness, small particle size and porous structure permit easy access for electrons and ions to the electrode/electrolyte, when the resulting materials are used as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries.  Electrochem. tests indicate that the Mo2C/GR hybrids exhibit much better lithium storage properties than pure GR and bulk Mo2C electrodes.  The enhanced electrochem. properties of the Mo2C/GR hybrids are mainly ascribed to the synergetic effects between Mo2C nanoparticles and the highly conductive GR support.  The results clearly demonstrate that the Mo2C/GR hybrids have potential application as anode materials in high-performance energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqUHhGePBSvRLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin5tcf6TWt2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXht1ajurvN&amp;md5=da410b58f4b668df7ac9a56e9f63ea8a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1021/nn303091t"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, Y.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional Carbon-Coated Graphene/Metal Oxide Hybrids for Enhanced Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Yuezeng; Li, Shuang; Wu, Dongqing; Zhang, Fan; Liang, Haiwei; Gao, Pengfei; Cheng, Chong; Feng, Xinliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8349-8356</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal oxides (MOs) have been widely investigated as promising high-capacity anode material for lithium ion batteries, but they usually exhibit poor cycling stability and rate performance due to the huge vol. change induced by the alloying reaction with lithium.  In this article, a double protection strategy is presented by fabricating a two-dimensional (2D) core-shell nanostructure to improve the electrochem. performance of metal oxides in lithium storage.  The 2D core-shell architecture is constructed by confining the well-defined graphene based metal oxides nanosheets (G@MO) within carbon layers.  The resulting 2D carbon-coated graphene/metal oxides nanosheets (G@MO@C) inherit the advantages of graphene, which possesses high elec. cond., large aspect ratio, and thin feature.  Furthermore, the carbon shells can tackle the deformation of MO nanoparticles while keeping the overall electrode highly conductive and active in lithium storage.  As the result, the produced G@MO@C hybrids exhibit outstanding reversible capacity and excellent rate performance for lithium storage (G@SnO2@C, 800 mAh g-1 at the rate of 200 mA g-1 after 100 cycles; G@Fe3O4@C, 920 mAh g-1 at the rate of 200 mA g-1 after 100 cycles).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQv7dfEDewv7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin5tcf6TWt2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xht1OksLfE&amp;md5=b470b12a2b8b4e4483482693bf5b1cc0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1021/nn4023894"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, X.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Green and Facile Fabrication of Hollow Porous MnO/C Microspheres from Microalgaes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xia, Yang; Xiao, Zhen; Dou, Xiao; Huang, Hui; Lu, Xianghong; Yan, Rongjun; Gan, Yongping; Zhu, Wenjun; Tu, Jiangping; Zhang, Wenkui; Tao, Xinyong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7083-7092</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow porous micro/nanostructures with high surface area and shell permeability have attracted tremendous attention.  Particularly, the synthesis and structural tailoring of diverse hollow porous materials is regarded as a crucial step toward the realization of high-performance electrode materials, which has several advantages including a large contact area with electrolyte, a superior structural stability, and a short transport path for Li+ ions.  Meanwhile, owing to the inexpensive, abundant, environmentally benign, and renewable biol. resources provided by nature, great efforts have been devoted to understand and practice the biotemplating technol., which was considered as an effective strategy to achieve morphol.-controllable materials with structural specialty, complexity, and related unique properties.  Herein, the authors are inspired by the natural microalgae with its special features (easy availability, biol. activity, and C sources) to develop a green and facile biotemplating method to fabricate monodisperse MnO/C microspheres for Li-ion batteries.  Due to the unique hollow porous structure in which MnO nanoparticles were tightly embedded into a porous C matrix and form a penetrative shell, MnO/C microspheres exhibited high reversible specific capacity of 700 mA-h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, excellent cycling stability with 94% capacity retention, and enhanced rate performance of 230 mA-h g-1 at 3 A g-1.  This green, sustainable, and economical strategy will extend the scope of biotemplating synthesis for exploring other functional materials in various structure-dependent applications such as catalysis, gas sensing, and energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpsQKzF09PBdLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin5tcf6TWt2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOqurfM&amp;md5=592dcca56bd411456287f5b12b2386e6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1039/C5RA01533B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.                         cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">QUANTUM ESPRESSO: a modular and open-source software project for quantum simulations of materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Giannozzi Paolo; Baroni Stefano; Bonini Nicola; Calandra Matteo; Car Roberto; Cavazzoni Carlo; Ceresoli Davide; Chiarotti Guido L; Cococcioni Matteo; Dabo Ismaila; Dal Corso Andrea; de Gironcoli Stefano; Fabris Stefano; Fratesi Guido; Gebauer Ralph; Gerstmann Uwe; Gougoussis Christos; Kokalj Anton; Lazzeri Michele; Martin-Samos Layla; Marzari Nicola; Mauri Francesco; Mazzarello Riccardo; Paolini Stefano; Pasquarello Alfredo; Paulatto Lorenzo; Sbraccia Carlo; Scandolo Sandro; Sclauzero Gabriele; Seitsonen Ari P; Smogunov Alexander; Umari Paolo; Wentzcovitch Renata M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of physics.     </div><div class="casAbstract">QUANTUM ESPRESSO is an integrated suite of computer codes for electronic-structure calculations and materials modeling, based on density-functional theory, plane waves, and pseudopotentials (norm-conserving, ultrasoft, and projector-augmented wave).  The acronym ESPRESSO stands for opEn Source Package for Research in Electronic Structure, Simulation, and Optimization.  It is freely available to researchers around the world under the terms of the GNU General Public License.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO builds upon newly-restructured electronic-structure codes that have been developed and tested by some of the original authors of novel electronic-structure algorithms and applied in the last twenty years by some of the leading materials modeling groups worldwide.  Innovation and efficiency are still its main focus, with special attention paid to massively parallel architectures, and a great effort being devoted to user friendliness.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO is evolving towards a distribution of independent and interoperable codes in the spirit of an open-source project, where researchers active in the field of electronic-structure calculations are encouraged to participate in the project by contributing their own codes or by implementing their own ideas into existing codes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcToTWfovXAMx7xanA7vODO6fW6udTcc2eYa-6fqnKz1uLntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3Mjltl2lug%253D%253D&amp;md5=da053fa748721b6b381051a20e7a7f53</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1016/j.commatsci.2013.08.053"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Garrity, K. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Vanderbilt, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudopotentials for High-throughput DFT Calculations</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Comput.                 10.1016/j.commatsci.2013.08.053</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D81%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D446-452%26journal%3DComput.%2BMater.%2BSci.%26author%3DK.%2BF.%2BGarrity%26author%3DJ.%2BW.%2BBennett%26author%3DK.%2BM.%2BRabe%26author%3DD.%2BVanderbilt%26title%3DPseudopotentials%2Bfor%2BHigh-throughput%2BDFT%2BCalculations%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.commatsci.2013.08.053&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b06625&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.commatsci.2013.08.053&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudopotentials for high-throughput DFT calculations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Garrity, Kevin F.; Bennett, Joseph W.; Rabe, Karin M.; Vanderbilt, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Computational Materials Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">81</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">446-452</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMMSEM</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0927-0256</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The increasing use of high-throughput d.-functional theory (DFT) calcns. in the computational design and optimization of materials requires the availability of a comprehensive set of soft and transferable pseudopotentials.  Here we present design criteria and testing results for a new open-source "GBRV" ultrasoft pseudopotential library that has been optimized for use in high-throughput DFT calcns.  We benchmark the GBRV potentials, as well as two other pseudopotential sets available in the literature, to all-electron calcns. in order to validate their accuracy.  The results allow us to draw conclusions about the accuracy of modern pseudopotentials in a variety of chem. environments.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoqrd9e14I8XrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liI6yHFWur2DQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFSku7vI&amp;md5=9900bae341b66a2e003ddf0b92fb7b97</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref59'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.100.136406"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Perdew, J.                 10.1103/PhysRevLett.100.136406</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D100%26publication_year%3D2008%26pages%3D136406-136409%26journal%3DPhys.%2BRev.%2BLett.%26author%3DJ.%2BP.%2BPerdew%26author%3DA.%2BRuzsinszky%26author%3DG.%2BI.%2BCsonka%26author%3DO.%2BA.%2BVydrov%26author%3DG.%2BE.%2BScuseria%26author%3DL.%2BA.%2BConstantin%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26author%3DK.%2BBurke%26title%3DRestoring%2Bthe%2BDensity-Gradient%2BExpansion%2Bfor%2BExchange%2Bin%2BSolids%2Band%2BSurfaces%26doi%3D10.1103%252FPhysRevLett.100.136406&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b06625&amp;doiOfLink=10.1103%2FPhysRevLett.100.136406&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Restoring the Density-Gradient Expansion for Exchange in Solids and Surfaces</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Perdew, John P.; Ruzsinszky, Adrienn; Csonka, Gabor I.; Vydrov, Oleg A.; Scuseria, Gustavo E.; Constantin, Lucian A.; Zhou, Xiaolan; Burke, Kieron</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">100</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">136406/1-136406/4</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRLTAO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0031-9007</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Popular modern generalized gradient approxns. are biased toward the description of free-atom energies.  Restoration of the first-principles gradient expansion for exchange over a wide range of d. gradients eliminates this bias.  We introduce a revised Perdew-Burke-Ernzerhof generalized gradient approxn. that improves equil. properties of densely packed solids and their surfaces.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a                         rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene Quantum Dots Coated VO2 Arrays for Highly Durable Electrodes for Li and Na Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Zhu, Changrong; Xia, Xinhui; Liu, Jilei; Zhang, Xiao; Wang, Jin; Liang, Pei; Lin, Jianyi; Zhang, Hua; Shen, Ze Xiang; Fan, Hong Jin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">565-573</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanoscale surface engineering is playing important role in enhancing the performance of battery electrode.  VO2 is one of high-capacity but less-stable materials and has been used mostly in the form of powders for Li-ion battery cathode with mediocre performance.  In this work, we design a new type of binder-free cathode by bottom-up growth of bifacial VO2 arrays directly on a graphene network for both high-performance Li-ion and Na-ion battery cathodes.  More importantly, graphene quantum dots are coated onto the VO2 surfaces as a highly efficient surface sensitizer and protection to further boost the electrochem. properties.  The integrated electrodes deliver a Na storage capacity of 306 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g, and a capacity of more than 110 mA-h/g after 1500 cycles at 18 A/g.  Our result on Na-ion battery may pave the way to next generation post-lithium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlNChWsQ5gnLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhOg4M5jZNkfQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFehsL7L&amp;md5=64c5ad4c1680e984a714a38620297d09</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA07452A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X. J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, X. J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">One-Dimensional Hybrid Nanocomposite of High-Density Monodispersed Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Nanoparticles and Carbon Nanotubes for High-Capacity Storage of Lithium and Sodium</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">18532</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">18542</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C6TA07452A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-dimensional hybrid nanocomposite of high-density monodispersed Fe3O4 nanoparticles and carbon nanotubes for high-capacity storage of lithium and sodium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiujuan; Liu, Xiaojie; Wang, Gang; Xia, Yuan; Wang, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18532-18542</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we report a simple but effective method to fill carbon nanotube (CNT) channels with a dense distribution of Fe3O4 nanoparticles, to produce Fe3O4@CNT.  The resulting novel heterogeneous nanostructure displayed multiple attractive features as an anode material in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  For example, this nanostructure displayed voids that apparently effectively prevented active material from aggregating and helped to accommodate their volumetric expansion during the cycling process.  In addn., most solid electrolyte interphases (SEIs) formed on the surfaces of the CNT shells instead of on individual Fe3O4 nanoparticles, limiting the amt. of SEIs and increasing the stability of the Fe3O4 nanoparticles.  As a result, when tested for LIBs, the Fe3O4@CNT nanocomposite exhibited an excellent rate capacity and cycling performance in half and full cells.  A high reversible capacity of 720 mA h g-1 was obtained after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1, and when the c.d. was increased to 8 A g-1, the specific capacity was 400 mA h g-1.  As for SIBs, a specific capacity of 377 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 was achieved after 300 cycles.  The facile synthetic route and unique nanostructure design may be extended to high-performance anode materials for LIBs and SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPJRClqmvTG7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYUXJx__O7aA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslGgsbrK&amp;md5=e63c2974a1c64aa5ee40bb0393e20173</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2013.03.019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xue, L. G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yildiz, O.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, G. W.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of CVD Carbon Coatings on Si@CNF Composite as Anode for Lithium-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">2</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">976</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">986</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2013.03.019</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of CVD carbon coatings on Si@CNF composite as anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fu, Kun; Xue, Leigang; Yildiz, Ozkan; Li, Shuli; Lee, Hun; Li, Ying; Xu, Guanjie; Zhou, Lan; Bradford, Philip D.; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">976-986</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-ion battery (LIB) anodes with high capacity and binder free structure were synthesized from carbon nanofibers that contained silicon nanoparticles (Si@CNF).  The particle filled nonwoven structures were produced by an electrospinning and subsequent carbonization process.  Pristine Si@CNF composites had Si nanoparticles exposed on the fiber surface.  As produced, the Si nanoparticles could become detached from the nanofiber surface during cycling, causing severe structural damage and capacity loss.  In order to prevent Si from detaching from the nanofiber surface, the Si@CNF composite was then treated with a thermal chem. vapor deposition (CVD) technique to make Si completely coated with a carbon matrix.  The carbon coated Si@CNF (Si@CNF-C) composites were synthesized with different Si contents (10, 30, and 50 wt%) for different CVD treatment times (30, 60, and 90 min).  It was found that the initial coulombic efficiency of Si@CNF-C could be increased via the amorphous carbon by stabilizing solid-electrolyte-interface (SEI) formation on surface.  The capacity and cyclic stability were improved by the CVD carbon coating, esp. for the 30 wt% Si@CNF-C composite with 90 min CVD coating, a CVD amorphous carbon coating of less than 1% by wt. on Si@CNF composites contributed to more than 200% improvement in cycling performance.  Results indicate that the CVD carbon coating is an effective approach to improve the electrochem. properties of Si@CNF composites making this a potential route to obtain high-energy d. anode materials for LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBBMJMVkR_crVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYUXJx__O7aA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXnt1Siu7c%253D&amp;md5=0dce47d324ae29daece33fb47d8e3109</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/C5NR01145K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hwang, S.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin oxide nanoparticles (SnO2 NPs) have been encapsulated in situ in a three-dimensional ordered space structure.  Within this composite, ordered mesoporous carbon (OMC) acts as a carbon framework showing a desirable ordered mesoporous structure with an av. pore size (≈6 nm) and a high surface area (470.3 m2/g), and the SnO2 NPs (≈10 nm) are highly loaded (up to 80 wt %) and homogeneously distributed within the OMC matrix.  As an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, a SnO2@OMC composite material can deliver an initial charge capacity of 943 mAh/g and retain 68.9 % of the initial capacity after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 50 mA/g, even exhibit a capacity of 503 mA h/g after 100 cycles at 160 mA/g.  In situ encapsulation of the SnO2 NPs within an OMC framework contributes to a higher capacity and a better cycling stability and rate capability in comparison with bare OMC and OMC ex situ loaded with SnO2 particles (SnO2/OMC).  The significantly improved electrochem. performance of the SnO2@OMC composite can be attributed to the multifunctional OMC matrix, which can facilitate electrolyte infiltration, accelerate charge transfer, and lithium-ion diffusion, and act as a favorable buffer to release reaction strains for lithiation/delithiation of the SnO2 NPs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqxWmCusogv67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYUXJx__O7aA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjtlKgurs%253D&amp;md5=0d2ea19484023c4ed37b0940eeb61a77</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b07450"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zuo, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion battery (SIB) is esp. attractive in cost-effective energy storage device as an alternative to lithium-ion battery.  Particularly, metal phosphides as potential anodes for SIBs have recently been demonstrated owing to their higher specific capacities compared with those of carbonaceous materials.  Unfortunately, most reported metal phosphides consist of irregular particles ranged from several hundreds nanometers to tens of micrometers, thus delivering limited cyclic stability.  This paper reports the sodium storage properties of additive-free Cu3P nanowire (CPNW) anode directly grown on copper current collector via an in situ growth followed by phosphidation method.  Therefore, as a result of its structure features, CPNW anode demonstrates highly stable cycling ability with an ≈70% retention in capacity at the 260th cycle, whereas most reported metal phosphides have limited cycle nos. ranged between 30 and 150.  Besides, the reaction mechanism between Cu3P and Na is investigated by examg. the intermediate products at different charge/discharge stages using ex situ X-ray diffraction measurements.  Furthermore, to explore the practical application of CPNW anode, a pouch-type Na+ full cell consisting of CPNW anode and Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode is assembled and characterized.  As a demonstration, a 10 cm × 10 cm light-emitting diode (LED) screen is successfully powered by the Na+ full cell.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJuwM8_tSmJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYUXJx__O7aA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XosVSlt74%253D&amp;md5=88fc2ecb8a32e8ed2bff3659fbc36cff</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1039/C6NR01774F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, P.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal phosphides are great promising anode materials for lithium-ion batteries with a high gravimetric capacity.  However, significant challenges such as low capacity, fast capacity fading and poor cycle stability must be addressed for their practical applications.  Herein, we demonstrate a versatile strategy for the synthesis of a novel three-dimensional porous molybdenum phosphide@carbon hybrid (3D porous MoP@C hybrid) by a template sol-gel method followed by an annealing treatment.  The resultant hybrid exhibits a 3D interconnected ordered porous structure with a relatively high surface area.  Benefiting from its advantages of microstructure and compn., the 3D porous MoP@C hybrid displays excellent lithium storage performance as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries in terms of specific capacity, cycling stability and long-cycle life.  It presents stable cycling performance with a high reversible capacity up to 1028 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  By ex situ XRD, HRTEM, SAED and XPS analyses, the 3D porous MoP@C hybrid was found to follow the Li-intercalation reaction mechanism (MoP + xLi+ + e- ↔ LixMoP), which was further confirmed by ab initio calcns. based on d. functional theory.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWT3_ZjreS2bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYUXJx__O7aA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xms1Wgt7w%253D&amp;md5=c20b89d86f145fa380ddb1f28cd91258</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2012.12.037"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanocryst. CoP thin film was prepd. by pulsed laser deposition and the electrochem. investigation of CoP as anode material for lithium-ion battery was reported.  The reversible discharge capacity of CoP/Li cell cycled between 0.1-3.0 V was found in the range of 788.0-1055.7 mA-h/g during the first 25 cycles.  A reversible couple of redox peaks at 0.63 and 1.02 V was obsd. in the first cycle of cyclic voltammetry curves.  Ex situ transmission electron microscopy and selected-area electron diffraction revealed the complete decompn. of CoP to Co/Li3P composite after discharging the CoP/Li cell to 0.1 V and the re-formation of CoP nanocryst. structure after recharging to 3.0 V, demonstrating a fully reversible conversion reaction mechanism between CoP and Co/Li3P composite.
