        </div><div class="casAbstract">Highly ordered mesostructured vanadium phosphonates (VP) were synthesized in the presence of cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) as a structure-directing agent.  Nitrilotris(methylene)triphosphonic acid (NMPA) and (ammonium/sodium) metavanadate (NH4VO3/NaVO3) were used for the construction of pore walls.  The CTAB templates are removed from the materials by an extn. process without destroying the parent mesostructure.  The formation mechanism for the ordered mesoporous structure and its impact on electrochem. application in lithium ion batteries (LIBs) are explained by considering the structural and electrochem. stability of the framework.  The results demonstrate that the counter cations (NH4+/Na+) of the metavanadate precursors have a crucial role in stabilizing the mesoporous structure of the mesoporous VP materials.  Mesoporous VP materials with highly ordered structure have great applicability as high-performance electrode materials in LIBs due to the advantages of their large contact area with electrolyte and short transport paths for lithium ions.  Mesoporous VP electrodes exhibit high reversible specific capacity with superb cycling stability (100 cycles) and excellent retention of capacity (92 %).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0SWZQQDMxUbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3zGNpOzQUow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktVeqsrs%253D&amp;md5=cda45714166a834764ed0dae1b0fa6fb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1021/cm800632f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A new family of mesoporous iron phosphonate (FeP) materials has been prepd. through cooperative assembly of cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB), iron nitrate, and nitrilotris(methylene)triphosphonic acid (NMPA).  CTAB is used as a structure directing agent, while the other two chems. are used as precursors for the formation of pore walls.  An extn. procedure is employed to remove the template without damaging the as-prepd. ordered mesostructure.  The obtained mesoporous FeP materials are well characterized by low angle X-ray diffraction (XRD), N2 adsorption isotherms, and transmission electron microscopy.  The mesostructural ordering of the obtained materials strongly depends on the synthetic conditions.  The morphol. and the crystallinity of the pore walls are investigated by SEM and wide-angle XRD measurements, resp.  It is revealed that the FeP framework is crystd. in the tetragonal crystal phase (I41/amd), according to the Rietveld refinement of the XRD patterns through the MAUD program.  The unit cell parameters of the obtained crystals are a = b = 5.1963 (3) Å, c = 12.9808 (1) Å (α = β = γ = 90°).  Also, the homogeneous distribution of both Fe species and organo-phosphonic acid groups in the mesoporous architectures is confirmed by Fourier transform IR spectroscopy and elemental mapping.  Mesoporous FeP materials with high surface area have great applicability as high performance electrode materials for lithium-ion (Li-ion) batteries, due to several advantages including a large contact area with the electrolyte, high structural stability, and short transport paths for Li+ ions.  Mesoporous FeP electrodes exhibit high reversible specific capacity with very good cycling stability and excellent retention of capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrC8oCzwWQrULVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3zGNpOzQUow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVOiur0%253D&amp;md5=ba8e0e4dfe92c692a0da164b2e3a0041</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1021/cm060433m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Boyanov, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bernardi, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gillot, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dupont, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Womes, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">FePy (y = 1, 2, 4) anodes all react with lithium through a conversion reaction FePy + 3yLi → yLi3P + Fe0 in their first discharge, leading to nanocomposite discharged electrodes described by nanosized Fe0 particles embedded in yLi3P matrixes.                         rightTab-cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoscaled Metal Borides and Phosphides: Recent Developments and Perspectives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Carenco, Sophie; Portehault, David; Boissiere, Cedric; Mezailles, Nicolas; Sanchez, Clement</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">113</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The wide variety of nanostructured metal boride and metal phosphide nanoparticles that can be obtained nowadays, and the strategies that researchers successfully developed to reach these nanoscaled phases are summarized.  The development of nanoscaled metal borides is clearly less mature essentially for two reasons: the lack of highly reactive boron sources and the resistance to crystn.  While mechanistic studies could shed light on the crucial exptl. levers for better compositional, structural, and morphol. control of nanostructured metal phosphides and metal borides, another tantalizing approach is to rethink the existing syntheses in terms of precursors, in an attempt to rationalize the stoichiometry introduced and the reaction temp.  The use of single-source precursors provides an interesting soln. by bringing the constituents in the right stoichiometry and already intertwined at the mol. scale.  A third path is to use very reactive P or B sources to ensure a quant. incorporation in the final nanomaterials.  The two families of materials are not mirrored in this aspect since elemental phosphorus P4 is highly reactive while elemental boron allotropes are very stable.  Relying on specific reaction media that can enhance kinetics, like specific solvents (e.g., salt melts) for metal borides, is another tempting soln.  The properties of nanoscaled metal borides and metal phosphides are shown to differ, if not outperform in some cases, those of the traditional bulk phases because of increased surface exposure or grain boundary d., and also confinement, like quantum effects in semiconductors.  The behavior of these nanoscaled cryst. phases in electronics, optics, magnetism, mechanics, and biomedicine are still to be explored, esp. because most of these compds. have not been obtained yet at the nanoscale in the strict sense: one particle dimension below 100 nm.  Future works may then first conc. on a better rationalization of the synthetic procedures, in order to further develop applications, for instance in the field of catalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoL1xza0rz5-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixuF_IMV9c3A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXpsFWru7k%253D&amp;md5=78ea6f2247dea47f9744aeef861c8338</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE02074C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kopold, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Aken, P.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal oxides have attracted considerable interest as promising anode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to their high energy densities.  It is necessary, however, to resolve the foremost issue for them in terms of practical applications, relating to the large vol. changes during cell operation.  Herein, we report a SnO2 anode with a hierarchical fibrous porous architecture which was fabricated by electrospinning the Sn-precursor with poly(vinylpyrrolidone) and subsequent temp.-dependent pyrolysis processes, resulting in the distinctive morphol., featuring hierarchical fibrous porous structures on the microscale with numerous primary constituent nanoparticles.  The porous fibers are composed of uniform polycryst. nanoparticles (approx. 10-50 nm in size) and abundant voids in close proximity to the constituent nanoparticles.  By comparing with an anode contg. com. SnO2 nanopowder (with a size of &lt;100 nm), we found that the porous fibrous SnO2 anode featured superior rate capability, long-term cycling stability, and dimensional stability, which was attributed to the distinctive structural characteristics, which offered enhanced kinetics towards electrochem. reactions with lithium ions and space for alleviating the huge vol. expansion during charging/discharging.  These findings would pave the way for practical applications in LIBs with high capacity and long cycle life of transition metal oxide anodes that suffer from significant vol. changes during cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpLSxfgeqB1-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixuF_IMV9c3A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsFOlsL%252FJ&amp;md5=bf4974d2ccab7ccdd89bc205b75aee0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201404161"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Asiri, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of effective and inexpensive hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) electrocatalysts for future renewable energy systems is highly desired.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Based on the concept of the nanoconfinement reaction, a synthetic strategy is developed to construct carbon-coated iron phosphide (FeP) with an amorphous and mesoporous framework anchored on carbon nanotubes (CNTs).  The synthesis involves direct growth of FeOOH on the CNTs followed by silica coating, carbon coating, and subsequent treatments of low-temp. phosphidation and silica removal procedures.  During the synthesis, the silica layer is adopted to not only serve as a sacrificial internal spacer to increase the mesoporosity (311 m2 g-1 and 0.36 cm3 g-1) of the FeP framework, but also to provide a confined environment in guiding the structural evolution of the homogenous/conformal framework and topol. amorphous nature of FeP.  When used as an anode material in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the FeP-based electrode shows a utilization rate of 78 % for the active material and a reversible capacity of 415 mAhg-1.  Even at a higher c.d. of 500 mAg-1, a capacity retention rate of 90 % over 500 cycles is obtained with a capacity-decay rate of only 0.02 % per cycle.  The much improved performance of the FeP-based electrode in SIBs clearly demonstrates the potential of FeP to be used as the anode material in SIBs when it is engineered in a nanoconfinement environment to overcome its structural constraints.  In principle, this strategy can be adapted to engineer other transition-metal phosphide-based materials for energy-storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrhob2dXIaDRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljt6FwD8-TL_w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XmvVSnurs%253D&amp;md5=b87d142360d08a67f3bfed67ecd9034f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.200600739"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Z.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel mesoporous-nanotube hybrid composite, namely mesoporous tin dioxide (SnO2) overlaying on the surface of multi-walled carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs), was prepd. by a simple method that included in situ growth of mesoporous SnO2 on the surface of MWCNTs through hydrothermal method utilizing Cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) as structure-directing agents. Results showed that the mesoporous-tube hybrid composites displayed higher capacity and better cycle performance in comparison with the mesoporous tin dioxide.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene sheets (one-atom-thick two-dimensional layers of sp2-bonded carbon) are predicted to have a range of unusual properties.  Their thermal cond. and mech. stiffness may rival the remarkable in-plane values for graphite (∼3000 W.m-1.K-1 and 1060 GPa, resp.); their fracture strength should be comparable to that of carbon nanotubes for similar types of defects; and recent studies have shown that individual graphene sheets have extraordinary electronic transport properties.  One possible route to harnessing these properties for applications would be to incorporate graphene sheets in a composite material.  The manufg. of such composites requires not only that graphene sheets be produced on a sufficient scale but that they also be incorporated, and homogeneously distributed, into various matrixes.  Graphite, inexpensive and available in large quantity, unfortunately does not readily exfoliate to yield individual graphene sheets.  Here we present a general approach for the prepn. of graphene-polymer composites via complete exfoliation of graphite and mol.-level dispersion of individual, chem. modified graphene sheets within polymer hosts.  A polystyrene-graphene composite formed by this route exhibits a percolation threshold of ∼0.1 vol.% for room-temp. elec. cond., the lowest reported value for any carbon-based composite except for those involving carbon nanotubes; at only 1 vol.%, this composite has a cond. of ∼0.1 S m-1, sufficient for many elec. applications.  Our bottom-up chem. approach of tuning the graphene sheet properties provides a path to a broad new class of graphene-based materials and their use in a variety of applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqiSXq1zKvbKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljt6FwD8-TL_w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XmvF2js7g%253D&amp;md5=f21ce86e81f2fd1e80ed987d0538188d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201603716"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene scroll is an emerging 1D tubular form of graphitic carbon that has potential applications in electrochem. energy storage.  However, it still remains a challenge to composite graphene scrolls with other nanomaterials for building advanced electrode configuration with fast and durable lithium storage properties.  Here, a transition-metal-oxide-based hierarchically ordered 3D porous electrode is designed based on assembling 1D core-sheath MnO@N-doped graphene scrolls with 2D N-doped graphene ribbons.  In the resulting architecture, porous MnO nanowires confined in tubular graphene scrolls are mech. isolated but electronically well-connected, while the interwoven graphene ribbons offer continuous conductive paths for electron transfer in all directions.  Moreover, the elastic graphene scrolls together with enough internal voids are able to accommodate the vol. expansion of the enclosed MnO.  Because of these merits, the as-built electrode manifests ultrahigh rate capability (349 mAh g-1 at 8.0 A g-1; 205 mAh g-1 at 15.0 A g-1) and robust cycling stability (812 mAh g-1 remaining after 1000 cycles at 2.0 A g-1) and is the most efficient MnO-based anode ever reported for lithium-ion batteries.  This unique multidimensional and hierarchically ordered structure design is believed to hold great potential in generalizable synthesis of graphene scrolls composited with oxide nanowires for mutifuctional energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqh8xcBh8-tE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-x-qjQa36hA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFenu7%252FM&amp;md5=632f9f9db962b375bfe78764a2077cd9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1021/jz201456p"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">By using carbon nanotubes (CNTs) as a shape template and glucose as a carbon precursor and structure-directing agent, CNT@Fe3O4@C porous core/sheath coaxial nanocables have been synthesized by a simple one-pot hydrothermal process.  Neither a surfactant/ligand nor a CNT pretreatment is needed in the synthesis process.  A possible growth mechanism governing the formation of this nanostructure is discussed.  When used as an anode material of lithium-ion batteries, the CNT@Fe3O4@C nanocables show significantly enhanced cycling performance, high rate capability, and high coulombic efficiency compared with pure Fe2O3 particles and Fe3O4/CNT composites.  The CNT@Fe3O4@C nanocables deliver a reversible capacity of 1290 mA-h/g after 80 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA/g, and maintain a reversible capacity of 690 mA-h/g after 200 cycles at a c.d. of 2000 mA/g.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe3O4, carbon-coated Fe3O4, and carbon-coated Fe3O4 embedded on carbon nanotubes are synthesized via hydrothermal reaction.  SEM anal. reveals that particle size of the as-synthesized Fe3O4 ranges from 100 to 250 nm, whereas carbon-coated Fe3O4 ranges from 10 to 15 nm in diam. and is surrounded by a thin carbon layer derived from sucrose.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel 3D hierarchical MoS2/graphene (MoS2/GN) composite is designed by a facile one-step hydrothermal co-assembling method without using any templates.  SEM and TEM images show that the MoS2/GN flower-like particles are self-assembled by MoS2 nanoflakes and graphene nanosheets.  According to the hydrothermal method used and characterization results obsd., the formation process is proposed.  Electrochem. performances of the MoS2/GN composite as anode active material in Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) is investigated in both MoS2/GN//Li half-cells and MoS2/GN//LiCoO2 full-cells.  The MoS2/GN composite delivers high initial discharge capacities of 1240 mAh g-1 and good capacity retentions (about 80%) after more than 80 cycles in half-cells.  Furthermore, the assembled MoS2/GN//LiCoO2 full-cell delivers high initial discharge capacities of 1203 mAh g-1.  The excellent lithium storage performances of the obtained MoS2/GN composite can be mainly attributed to the designed novel structure of the composite.  The cross-linked graphene nanosheets, the anchoring MoS2 nanoflakes and the synergistic effects between them make the composite good cond., enough buffering space for the vol. change, and shortened ionic transport length.  This work clearly demonstrates that the MoS2/GN composite is a promising alternative material for anode in the LIB applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq1SBxs6HfMYbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-VXGC9OFx4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFajsLrM&amp;md5=f4352d4ffbe464f6bbfedd316c4f3b4d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2004.08.033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Okpalugo, T. XPS anal. of chem. functionalized multi-wall carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs) and single-wall carbon nanotubes (SWCNT) was done with ESCA300 (overall instrument resoln. of 0.35 eV).  Information to the degree of functionalization was ascertained by argon ion bombardment of the samples followed by XPS anal. to detect the functional groups, the percentage at. concn. of various elements present and whether or not the detected functional groups imposed a chem. shift on the CNT atoms.  The results show that true chem. functionalization was achieved and by argon ion bombardment can alter these functional groups relative to the C 1s carbon atoms of the CNT. The carbon atom on the nanotube ring to which the functional group (atom) is bonded, the chirality of the CNT, the electronegativity of the functional group, the bond type and whether the CNT is single-wall or multi-wall, or cut (short) could play a role in detg. the chem. shift on the CNTs atoms. Such purposely designed hybrid nanostructures have an enhanced electronic/ionic cond., stable electrode/electrolyte interface, and phys. buffering effect arising from the nanoscale combination of carbon with Fe3O4, as well as the hollow, aligned and hierarchically porous architectures.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Magnetite (Fe3O4) is an attractive electrode material due to its high theor. capacity, eco-friendliness, and natural abundance.  However, its com. application in Li-ion batteries is still hindered by its poor cycling stability and low rate capacity resulting from large vol. expansion and low cond.  The authors present a new approach which makes use of supercrit. CO2 to efficiently anchor Fe3O4 nanoparticles (NPs) on graphene foam (GF), which was obtained by CVD in a single step.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal oxides (MOs) have been widely investigated as promising high-capacity anode material for lithium ion batteries, but they usually exhibit poor cycling stability and rate performance due to the huge vol. change induced by the alloying reaction with lithium.  In this article, a double protection strategy is presented by fabricating a two-dimensional (2D) core-shell nanostructure to improve the electrochem. performance of metal oxides in lithium storage.  The 2D core-shell architecture is constructed by confining the well-defined graphene based metal oxides nanosheets (G@MO) within carbon layers.  The resulting 2D carbon-coated graphene/metal oxides nanosheets (G@MO@C) inherit the advantages of graphene, which possesses high elec. cond., large aspect ratio, and thin feature.  Furthermore, the carbon shells can tackle the deformation of MO nanoparticles while keeping the overall electrode highly conductive and active in lithium storage.  As the result, the produced G@MO@C hybrids exhibit outstanding reversible capacity and excellent rate performance for lithium storage (G@SnO2@C, 800 mAh g-1 at the rate of 200 mA g-1 after 100 cycles; G@Fe3O4@C, 920 mAh g-1 at the rate of 200 mA g-1 after 100 cycles).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQv7dfEDewv7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liC1AUsBUZhPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xht1OksLfE&amp;md5=b470b12a2b8b4e4483482693bf5b1cc0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref55" class="rightTabRefNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit55" data-doi="10.1021/nn4023894"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, X.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow porous micro/nanostructures with high surface area and shell permeability have attracted tremendous attention.  Particularly, the synthesis and structural tailoring of diverse hollow porous materials is regarded as a crucial step toward the realization of high-performance electrode materials, which has several advantages including a large contact area with electrolyte, a superior structural stability, and a short transport path for Li+ ions.  Meanwhile, owing to the inexpensive, abundant, environmentally benign, and renewable biol. resources provided by nature, great efforts have been devoted to understand and practice the biotemplating technol., which was considered as an effective strategy to achieve morphol.-controllable materials with structural specialty, complexity, and related unique properties.  Herein, the authors are inspired by the natural microalgae with its special features (easy availability, biol. activity, and C sources) to develop a green and facile biotemplating method to fabricate monodisperse MnO/C microspheres for Li-ion batteries.  Due to the unique hollow porous structure in which MnO nanoparticles were tightly embedded into a porous C matrix and form a penetrative shell, MnO/C microspheres exhibited high reversible specific capacity of 700 mA-h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, excellent cycling stability with 94% capacity retention, and enhanced rate performance of 230 mA-h g-1 at 3 A g-1.  This green, sustainable, and economical strategy will extend the scope of biotemplating synthesis for exploring other functional materials in various structure-dependent applications such as catalysis, gas sensing, and energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpsQKzF09PBdLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liC1AUsBUZhPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOqurfM&amp;md5=592dcca56bd411456287f5b12b2386e6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref56" class="rightTabRefNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit56" data-doi="10.1039/C5RA01533B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J. X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of Free-Standing Reduced Graphene Oxide Membranes with Different Thicknesses and Comparison of Their Electrochemical Performance as Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">RSC Adv.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">30084</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">30091</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C5RA01533B</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref57" class="rightTabRefNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit57" data-doi="10.1088/0953-8984/21/39/395502"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Giannozzi, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Baroni, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bonini, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Calandra, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Car, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cavazzoni, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ceresoli, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guido, L. C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cococcioni, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dabo, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Corso, A. D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fabris, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fratesi, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">de Gironcoli, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gebauer, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gerstmann, U.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gougoussis, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kokalj, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lazzeri, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Martin-Samos, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Marzari, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mauri, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mazzarello, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Paolini, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pasquarello, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Paulatto, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sbraccia, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Scandolo, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sclauzero, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Seitsonen, A. P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Smogunov, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Umari, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wentzcovitch, R. M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">QUANTUM ESPRESSO: A Modular and Open-Source Software Project for Quantum Simulations of Materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Phys.: Condens. Matter</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2009</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">21</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">395502</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">395521</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1088/0953-8984/21/39/395502</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">QUANTUM ESPRESSO: a modular and open-source software project for quantum simulations of materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Giannozzi Paolo; Baroni Stefano; Bonini Nicola; Calandra Matteo; Car Roberto; Cavazzoni Carlo; Ceresoli Davide; Chiarotti Guido L; Cococcioni Matteo; Dabo Ismaila; Dal Corso Andrea; de Gironcoli Stefano; Fabris Stefano; Fratesi Guido; Gebauer Ralph; Gerstmann Uwe; Gougoussis Christos; Kokalj Anton; Lazzeri Michele; Martin-Samos Layla; Marzari Nicola; Mauri Francesco; Mazzarello Riccardo; Paolini Stefano; Pasquarello Alfredo; Paulatto Lorenzo; Sbraccia Carlo; Scandolo Sandro; Sclauzero Gabriele; Seitsonen Ari P; Smogunov Alexander; Umari Paolo; Wentzcovitch Renata M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of physics. Condensed matter : an Institute of Physics journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">39</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">395502</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">QUANTUM ESPRESSO is an integrated suite of computer codes for electronic-structure calculations and materials modeling, based on density-functional theory, plane waves, and pseudopotentials (norm-conserving, ultrasoft, and projector-augmented wave).  The acronym ESPRESSO stands for opEn Source Package for Research in Electronic Structure, Simulation, and Optimization.  It is freely available to researchers around the world under the terms of the GNU General Public License.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO builds upon newly-restructured electronic-structure codes that have been developed and tested by some of the original authors of novel electronic-structure algorithms and applied in the last twenty years by some of the leading materials modeling groups worldwide.  Innovation and efficiency are still its main focus, with special attention paid to massively parallel architectures, and a great effort being devoted to user friendliness.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO is evolving towards a distribution of independent and interoperable codes in the spirit of an open-source project, where researchers active in the field of electronic-structure calculations are encouraged to participate in the project by contributing their own codes or by implementing their own ideas into existing codes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcToTWfovXAMx7xanA7vODO6fW6udTcc2eZP0bQxkPrxvbntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3Mjltl2lug%253D%253D&amp;md5=da053fa748721b6b381051a20e7a7f53</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref58" class="rightTabRefNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit58" data-doi="10.1016/j.commatsci.2013.08.053"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Garrity, K. F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bennett, J. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rabe, K. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Vanderbilt, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudopotentials for High-throughput DFT Calculations</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Comput. Mater. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">81</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">446</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">452</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.commatsci.2013.08.053</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudopotentials for high-throughput DFT calculations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Garrity, Kevin F.; Bennett, Joseph W.; Rabe, Karin M.; Vanderbilt, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Computational Materials Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">81</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">446-452</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMMSEM</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0927-0256</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The increasing use of high-throughput d.-functional theory (DFT) calcns. in the computational design and optimization of materials requires the availability of a comprehensive set of soft and transferable pseudopotentials.  Here we present design criteria and testing results for a new open-source "GBRV" ultrasoft pseudopotential library that has been optimized for use in high-throughput DFT calcns.  We benchmark the GBRV potentials, as well as two other pseudopotential sets available in the literature, to all-electron calcns. in order to validate their accuracy.  The results allow us to draw conclusions about the accuracy of modern pseudopotentials in a variety of chem. environments.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoqrd9e14I8XrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhixNJ1UvnGLw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFSku7vI&amp;md5=9900bae341b66a2e003ddf0b92fb7b97</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref59" class="rightTabRefNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit59" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.100.136406"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Perdew, J. P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ruzsinszky, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Csonka, G. I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Vydrov, O. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Scuseria, G. E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Constantin, L. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Burke, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Restoring the Density-Gradient Expansion for Exchange in Solids and Surfaces</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys. Rev. Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2008</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">100</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">136406</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">136409</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1103/PhysRevLett.100.136406</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Restoring the Density-Gradient Expansion for Exchange in Solids and Surfaces</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Perdew, John P.; Ruzsinszky, Adrienn; Csonka, Gabor I.; Vydrov, Oleg A.; Scuseria, Gustavo E.; Constantin, Lucian A.; Zhou, Xiaolan; Burke, Kieron</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">100</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">136406/1-136406/4</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRLTAO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0031-9007</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Popular modern generalized gradient approxns. are biased toward the description of free-atom energies.  Restoration of the first-principles gradient expansion for exchange over a wide range of d. gradients eliminates this bias.  We introduce a revised Perdew-Burke-Ernzerhof generalized gradient approxn. that improves equil. properties of densely packed solids and their surfaces.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoO4aw1yPkdOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhixNJ1UvnGLw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1cXktlygt7c%253D&amp;md5=bb5e35a295ab7af85d65ac410d6f898c</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i15">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsnano.7b06625" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsnano.7b06625</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Characterizations of XRD, SEM, TEM, HRTEM, SAED, surface wettability, and electrical conductivities for prepared materials; electrochemical measurements including CV curves, cycling performances, and rate capabilities of FeP-based materials (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.7b06625/suppl_file/nn7b06625_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.7b06625/suppl_file/nn7b06625_si_001.pdf">nn7b06625_si_001.pdf (4.01 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

        <script nonce="90f6ee100a91775c-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="90f6ee100a91775c-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6ee100a91775c-SJC">
"use strict"

	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6ee100a91775c-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Nano";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");
                });
                
            } else {
                    cookie=status;
            }

            cookie1 = cookie;
            cookie = cookie1 + "; path=/; domain=.acs.org";
            //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
            $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
            console.log("ACSPubs2 success");
    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
        cookie="error: 127.0.0.1";
        //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
        $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
        console.log("ACSPubs2 failed");
        //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
    });
});
